<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6c9696733174498590479b033c26f3ff"><span data-offset-key="6c9696733174498590479b033c26f3ff:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">‚Äã</span></span></span><a href="https://www.notion.so/f133bdfd160d419b80d2028341628263" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="63269d53974b436aabe3384111393a38"><span data-offset-key="63269d53974b436aabe3384111393a38:0">Builtin Methods</span></span></a><span data-key="52e100e7c13c4b0ea9b1b53822c80bde"><span data-offset-key="52e100e7c13c4b0ea9b1b53822c80bde:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">‚Äã</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dc249f9466da42f798691cd8902cd82e"><span data-offset-key="dc249f9466da42f798691cd8902cd82e:0">**`abs`**</span><span data-offset-key="dc249f9466da42f798691cd8902cd82e:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="dc249f9466da42f798691cd8902cd82e:2">*x*</span><span data-offset-key="dc249f9466da42f798691cd8902cd82e:3">)Return the absolute value of a number. The argument may be an integer, a floating point number, or an object implementing </span><span data-offset-key="dc249f9466da42f798691cd8902cd82e:4">`[__abs__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__abs__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="dc249f9466da42f798691cd8902cd82e:5">. If the argument is a complex number, its magnitude is returned.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2d73c27668164b3fbf4b2fe910b8f5b2"><span data-offset-key="2d73c27668164b3fbf4b2fe910b8f5b2:0">**`all`**</span><span data-offset-key="2d73c27668164b3fbf4b2fe910b8f5b2:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="2d73c27668164b3fbf4b2fe910b8f5b2:2">*iterable*</span><span data-offset-key="2d73c27668164b3fbf4b2fe910b8f5b2:3">)Return </span><span data-offset-key="2d73c27668164b3fbf4b2fe910b8f5b2:4">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="2d73c27668164b3fbf4b2fe910b8f5b2:5"> if all elements of the </span><span data-offset-key="2d73c27668164b3fbf4b2fe910b8f5b2:6">*iterable*</span><span data-offset-key="2d73c27668164b3fbf4b2fe910b8f5b2:7"> are true (or if the iterable is empty). Equivalent to:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="42b0655a84a74b88864e40a8776c1768"><span data-offset-key="42b0655a84a74b88864e40a8776c1768:0">\*\*</span><span data-offset-key="42b0655a84a74b88864e40a8776c1768:1">`def** all(iterable): **for** element **in** iterable: **if** **not** element: **return** **Falsereturn** **True**`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bc40a0c403dd439d87abe19cc2971330"><span data-offset-key="bc40a0c403dd439d87abe19cc2971330:0">**`any`**</span><span data-offset-key="bc40a0c403dd439d87abe19cc2971330:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="bc40a0c403dd439d87abe19cc2971330:2">*iterable*</span><span data-offset-key="bc40a0c403dd439d87abe19cc2971330:3">)Return </span><span data-offset-key="bc40a0c403dd439d87abe19cc2971330:4">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="bc40a0c403dd439d87abe19cc2971330:5"> if any element of the </span><span data-offset-key="bc40a0c403dd439d87abe19cc2971330:6">*iterable*</span><span data-offset-key="bc40a0c403dd439d87abe19cc2971330:7"> is true. If the iterable is empty, return </span><span data-offset-key="bc40a0c403dd439d87abe19cc2971330:8">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="bc40a0c403dd439d87abe19cc2971330:9">. Equivalent to:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1173b56d63b047488d31e4d96bba5401"><span data-offset-key="1173b56d63b047488d31e4d96bba5401:0">\*\*</span><span data-offset-key="1173b56d63b047488d31e4d96bba5401:1">`def** any(iterable): **for** element **in** iterable: **if** element: **return** **Truereturn** **False**`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25"><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:0">**`ascii`**</span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:2">*object*</span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:3">)As </span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:4">`[repr()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#repr>)`</span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:5">, return a string containing a printable representation of an object, but escape the non-ASCII characters in the string returned by </span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:6">`[repr()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#repr>)`</span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:7"> using </span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:8">`\\x`</span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:9">, </span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:10">`\\u`</span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:11"> or </span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:12">`\\U`</span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:13"> escapes. This generates a string similar to that returned by </span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:14">`[repr()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#repr>)`</span><span data-offset-key="fe8e96b2013a4f69bf62d58aad18db25:15"> in Python 2.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="23a7defc71014c2a86ec1ec6b51e8902"><span data-offset-key="23a7defc71014c2a86ec1ec6b51e8902:0">**`bin`**</span><span data-offset-key="23a7defc71014c2a86ec1ec6b51e8902:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="23a7defc71014c2a86ec1ec6b51e8902:2">*x*</span><span data-offset-key="23a7defc71014c2a86ec1ec6b51e8902:3">)Convert an integer number to a binary string prefixed with ‚Äú0b‚Äù. The result is a valid Python expression. If </span><span data-offset-key="23a7defc71014c2a86ec1ec6b51e8902:4">*x*</span><span data-offset-key="23a7defc71014c2a86ec1ec6b51e8902:5"> is not a Python </span><span data-offset-key="23a7defc71014c2a86ec1ec6b51e8902:6">`[int](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int>)`</span><span data-offset-key="23a7defc71014c2a86ec1ec6b51e8902:7"> object, it has to define an </span><span data-offset-key="23a7defc71014c2a86ec1ec6b51e8902:8">`[__index__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__index__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="23a7defc71014c2a86ec1ec6b51e8902:9"> method that returns an integer. Some examples:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d7172665ef0d443bb92e938e6c350d85"><span data-offset-key="d7172665ef0d443bb92e938e6c350d85:0">\*\*</span><span data-offset-key="d7172665ef0d443bb92e938e6c350d85:1">`>>>** bin(3) '0b11' **>>>** bin(-10) '-0b1010'`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="55b32fcd08124992b1759e14d973845f"><span data-offset-key="55b32fcd08124992b1759e14d973845f:0">If prefix ‚Äú0b‚Äù is desired or not, you can use either of the following ways.&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7e8e7c7cb5494c9680fe2c6d9ba59c8e"><span data-offset-key="7e8e7c7cb5494c9680fe2c6d9ba59c8e:0">\*\*</span><span data-offset-key="7e8e7c7cb5494c9680fe2c6d9ba59c8e:1">`>>>** format(14, '#b'), format(14, 'b') ('0b1110', '1110') **>>>** f'*{*14*:*#b*}*', f'*{*14*:*b*}*' ('0b1110', '1110')`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fe59a0b1011d4742ac03ac59e186be16"><span data-offset-key="fe59a0b1011d4742ac03ac59e186be16:0">See also </span><span data-offset-key="fe59a0b1011d4742ac03ac59e186be16:1">`[format()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#format>)`</span><span data-offset-key="fe59a0b1011d4742ac03ac59e186be16:2"> for more information.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd"><span data-offset-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd:0">*class*</span><span data-offset-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd:1"> </span><span data-offset-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd:2">**`bool`**</span><span data-offset-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd:3">(\[</span><span data-offset-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd:4">*x*</span><span data-offset-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd:5">\])Return a Boolean value, i.e. one of </span><span data-offset-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd:6">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd:7"> or </span><span data-offset-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd:8">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd:9">. </span><span data-offset-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd:10">*x*</span><span data-offset-key="2127e85b28214ac5a0f39e15dfb6cedd:11"> is converted using the standard </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#truth" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b8ec620064fa44a19062847974ffe9db"><span data-offset-key="b8ec620064fa44a19062847974ffe9db:0">truth testing procedure</span></span></a><span data-key="7ba659b765b5403a8130eed8c4558746"><span data-offset-key="7ba659b765b5403a8130eed8c4558746:0">. If </span><span data-offset-key="7ba659b765b5403a8130eed8c4558746:1">*x*</span><span data-offset-key="7ba659b765b5403a8130eed8c4558746:2"> is false or omitted, this returns </span><span data-offset-key="7ba659b765b5403a8130eed8c4558746:3">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="7ba659b765b5403a8130eed8c4558746:4">; otherwise it returns </span><span data-offset-key="7ba659b765b5403a8130eed8c4558746:5">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="7ba659b765b5403a8130eed8c4558746:6">. The </span><span data-offset-key="7ba659b765b5403a8130eed8c4558746:7">`[bool](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool>)`</span><span data-offset-key="7ba659b765b5403a8130eed8c4558746:8"> class is a subclass of </span><span data-offset-key="7ba659b765b5403a8130eed8c4558746:9">`[int](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int>)`</span><span data-offset-key="7ba659b765b5403a8130eed8c4558746:10"> (see </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#typesnumeric" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9ba04610c4d64ba586c431b8d3be35f5"><span data-offset-key="9ba04610c4d64ba586c431b8d3be35f5:0">Numeric Types ‚Äî int, float, complex</span></span></a><span data-key="fbc33e0ce2cd4545af0d475935c0d6dd"><span data-offset-key="fbc33e0ce2cd4545af0d475935c0d6dd:0">). It cannot be subclassed further. Its only instances are </span><span data-offset-key="fbc33e0ce2cd4545af0d475935c0d6dd:1">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="fbc33e0ce2cd4545af0d475935c0d6dd:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="fbc33e0ce2cd4545af0d475935c0d6dd:3">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="fbc33e0ce2cd4545af0d475935c0d6dd:4"> (see </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#bltin-boolean-values" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a6111b5bf3264d8fb06086a8ecb01d5d"><span data-offset-key="a6111b5bf3264d8fb06086a8ecb01d5d:0">Boolean Values</span></span></a><span data-key="1caaf19b5501487b8d00a9ad1e2b3a3e"><span data-offset-key="1caaf19b5501487b8d00a9ad1e2b3a3e:0">). </span><span data-offset-key="1caaf19b5501487b8d00a9ad1e2b3a3e:1">*Changed in version 3.7: x*</span><span data-offset-key="1caaf19b5501487b8d00a9ad1e2b3a3e:2"> is now a positional-only parameter.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05"><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:0">**`breakpoint`**</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:1">(\*</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:2">*args*</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:3">, \*\*</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:4">*kws*</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:5">)This function drops you into the debugger at the call site. Specifically, it calls </span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:6">`[sys.breakpointhook()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#sys.breakpointhook>)`</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:7">, passing </span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:8">`args`</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:9"> and </span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:10">`kws`</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:11"> straight through. By default, </span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:12">`sys.breakpointhook()`</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:13"> calls </span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:14">`[pdb.set_trace()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/pdb.html#pdb.set_trace>)`</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:15"> expecting no arguments. In this case, it is purely a convenience function so you don‚Äôt have to explicitly import </span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:16">`[pdb](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/pdb.html#module-pdb>)`</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:17"> or type as much code to enter the debugger. However, </span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:18">`[sys.breakpointhook()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#sys.breakpointhook>)`</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:19"> can be set to some other function and </span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:20">`[breakpoint()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#breakpoint>)`</span><span data-offset-key="3f02afd891d8408cb4b6b853986e6b05:21"> will automatically call that, allowing you to drop into the debugger of choice. Raises an </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#auditing" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f68a16f6d03f4ffc871d6e3071c68e91"><span data-offset-key="f68a16f6d03f4ffc871d6e3071c68e91:0">auditing event</span></span></a><span data-key="f252c547bd9c4112b1eba68f1b7a89ab"><span data-offset-key="f252c547bd9c4112b1eba68f1b7a89ab:0"> </span><span data-offset-key="f252c547bd9c4112b1eba68f1b7a89ab:1">`builtins.breakpoint`</span><span data-offset-key="f252c547bd9c4112b1eba68f1b7a89ab:2"> with argument </span><span data-offset-key="f252c547bd9c4112b1eba68f1b7a89ab:3">`breakpointhook`</span><span data-offset-key="f252c547bd9c4112b1eba68f1b7a89ab:4">. </span><span data-offset-key="f252c547bd9c4112b1eba68f1b7a89ab:5">*New in version 3.7.*</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d"><span data-offset-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d:0">*class*</span><span data-offset-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d:1"> </span><span data-offset-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d:2">**`bytearray`**</span><span data-offset-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d:3">(\[</span><span data-offset-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d:4">*source*</span><span data-offset-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d:5">\[, </span><span data-offset-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d:6">*encoding*</span><span data-offset-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d:7">\[, </span><span data-offset-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d:8">*errors*</span><span data-offset-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d:9">\]\]\])Return a new array of bytes. The </span><span data-offset-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d:10">`[bytearray](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#bytearray>)`</span><span data-offset-key="52b3b9e51a5f4e5c96b453b64eef2d0d:11"> class is a mutable sequence of integers in the range 0 &lt;= x &lt; 256. It has most of the usual methods of mutable sequences, described in </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#typesseq-mutable" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="7113dd23eaaf4e889e689bccce2832e4"><span data-offset-key="7113dd23eaaf4e889e689bccce2832e4:0">Mutable Sequence Types</span></span></a><span data-key="6d7283dcf80e4643afe964c1628df916"><span data-offset-key="6d7283dcf80e4643afe964c1628df916:0">, as well as most methods that the </span><span data-offset-key="6d7283dcf80e4643afe964c1628df916:1">`[bytes](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#bytes>)`</span><span data-offset-key="6d7283dcf80e4643afe964c1628df916:2"> type has, see </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#bytes-methods" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="27f3297740cd4e73ba6b5203af731c1e"><span data-offset-key="27f3297740cd4e73ba6b5203af731c1e:0">Bytes and Bytearray Operations</span></span></a><span data-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed"><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:0">. The optional </span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:1">*source*</span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:2"> parameter can be used to initialize the array in a few different ways: ‚Ä¢ If it is a </span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:3">*string*</span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:4">, you must also give the </span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:5">*encoding*</span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:6"> (and optionally, </span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:7">*errors*</span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:8">) parameters; </span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:9">`[bytearray()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#bytearray>)`</span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:10"> then converts the string to bytes using </span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:11">`[str.encode()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str.encode>)`</span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:12">. ‚Ä¢ If it is an </span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:13">*integer*</span><span data-offset-key="e901bb00b7474ff5b7d6a7e640f0d3ed:14">, the array will have that size and will be initialized with null bytes. ‚Ä¢ If it is an object conforming to the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/c-api/buffer.html#bufferobjects" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b32cd124d37944cbbc8c1871f4dc5703"><span data-offset-key="b32cd124d37944cbbc8c1871f4dc5703:0">buffer interface</span></span></a><span data-key="8ca75edd5d84405fa58410c881531093"><span data-offset-key="8ca75edd5d84405fa58410c881531093:0">, a read-only buffer of the object will be used to initialize the bytes array. ‚Ä¢ If it is an </span><span data-offset-key="8ca75edd5d84405fa58410c881531093:1">*iterable*</span><span data-offset-key="8ca75edd5d84405fa58410c881531093:2">, it must be an iterable of integers in the range </span><span data-offset-key="8ca75edd5d84405fa58410c881531093:3">`0 <= x < 256`</span><span data-offset-key="8ca75edd5d84405fa58410c881531093:4">, which are used as the initial contents of the array. Without an argument, an array of size 0 is created. See also </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#binaryseq" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6940e83f61c24207977f212889d1ad46"><span data-offset-key="6940e83f61c24207977f212889d1ad46:0">Binary Sequence Types ‚Äî bytes, bytearray, memoryview</span></span></a><span data-key="689be19a4869415fafef808ee897d41b"><span data-offset-key="689be19a4869415fafef808ee897d41b:0"> and </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#typebytearray" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="01ecfd5d037a44e1b2b01fa94607a20c"><span data-offset-key="01ecfd5d037a44e1b2b01fa94607a20c:0">Bytearray Objects</span></span></a><span data-key="379d98c049d243788eba316923270162"><span data-offset-key="379d98c049d243788eba316923270162:0">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649"><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:0">*class*</span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:1"> </span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:2">**`bytes`**</span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:3">(\[</span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:4">*source*</span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:5">\[, </span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:6">*encoding*</span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:7">\[, </span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:8">*errors*</span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:9">\]\]\])Return a new ‚Äúbytes‚Äù object, which is an immutable sequence of integers in the range </span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:10">`0 <= x < 256`</span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:11">. </span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:12">`[bytes](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#bytes>)`</span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:13"> is an immutable version of </span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:14">`[bytearray](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#bytearray>)`</span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:15"> ‚Äì it has the same non-mutating methods and the same indexing and slicing behavior. Accordingly, constructor arguments are interpreted as for </span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:16">`[bytearray()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#bytearray>)`</span><span data-offset-key="a30c48231f824764bb70db9659151649:17">. Bytes objects can also be created with literals, see </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/lexical_analysis.html#strings" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d6ec5ea7a6bd41f98c04a357520bc093"><span data-offset-key="d6ec5ea7a6bd41f98c04a357520bc093:0">String and Bytes literals</span></span></a><span data-key="3494ca73e01a4e2685e509f1d993d1ea"><span data-offset-key="3494ca73e01a4e2685e509f1d993d1ea:0">. See also </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#binaryseq" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6874fbd4237941b683d9e8b2f619981c"><span data-offset-key="6874fbd4237941b683d9e8b2f619981c:0">Binary Sequence Types ‚Äî bytes, bytearray, memoryview</span></span></a><span data-key="b3ca1d6f2bdd41198fb30c74a1c5131c"><span data-offset-key="b3ca1d6f2bdd41198fb30c74a1c5131c:0">, </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#typebytes" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="65d9e2c1448f4c658bee0f81a44c172a"><span data-offset-key="65d9e2c1448f4c658bee0f81a44c172a:0">Bytes Objects</span></span></a><span data-key="0031a7058ff246cfb42253f5ff7f6f81"><span data-offset-key="0031a7058ff246cfb42253f5ff7f6f81:0">, and </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#bytes-methods" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ede60b027e384219be1aa859fca010fb"><span data-offset-key="ede60b027e384219be1aa859fca010fb:0">Bytes and Bytearray Operations</span></span></a><span data-key="2861b8645d9f469ba5fdca7bc5874bad"><span data-offset-key="2861b8645d9f469ba5fdca7bc5874bad:0">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f"><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:0">**`callable`**</span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:2">*object*</span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:3">)Return </span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:4">`[True](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#True>)`</span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:5"> if the </span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:6">*object*</span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:7"> argument appears callable, </span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:8">`[False](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#False>)`</span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:9"> if not. If this returns </span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:10">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:11">, it is still possible that a call fails, but if it is </span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:12">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:13">, calling </span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:14">*object*</span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:15"> will never succeed. Note that classes are callable (calling a class returns a new instance); instances are callable if their class has a </span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:16">`[__call__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__call__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:17"> method. </span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:18">*New in version 3.2:*</span><span data-offset-key="3aff8409db784c7896cc94b9ef69da1f:19"> This function was first removed in Python 3.0 and then brought back in Python 3.2.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c"><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:0">**`chr`**</span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:2">*i*</span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:3">)Return the string representing a character whose Unicode code point is the integer </span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:4">*i*</span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:5">. For example, </span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:6">`chr(97)`</span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:7"> returns the string </span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:8">`'a'`</span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:9">, while </span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:10">`chr(8364)`</span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:11"> returns the string </span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:12">`'‚Ç¨'`</span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:13">. This is the inverse of </span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:14">`[ord()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#ord>)`</span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:15">. The valid range for the argument is from 0 through 1,114,111 (0x10FFFF in base 16). </span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:16">`[ValueError](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/exceptions.html#ValueError>)`</span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:17"> will be raised if </span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:18">*i*</span><span data-offset-key="6bfd2ded6f8a4977b5213e5b45157c9c:19"> is outside that range.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="90939cb0e79e4c3aab2a2429f1c8b548"><span data-offset-key="90939cb0e79e4c3aab2a2429f1c8b548:0">`@**classmethod**`</span><span data-offset-key="90939cb0e79e4c3aab2a2429f1c8b548:1">Transform a method into a class method. A class method receives the class as implicit first argument, just like an instance method receives the instance. To declare a class method, use this idiom:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5263b266451041a5b45e275051a90f8e"><span data-offset-key="5263b266451041a5b45e275051a90f8e:0">\*\*</span><span data-offset-key="5263b266451041a5b45e275051a90f8e:1">`class** **C**: **@classmethoddef** f(cls, arg1, arg2, ...): ...`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0608be73907e42769d6692e58d62753f"><span data-offset-key="0608be73907e42769d6692e58d62753f:0">The </span><span data-offset-key="0608be73907e42769d6692e58d62753f:1">`@classmethod`</span><span data-offset-key="0608be73907e42769d6692e58d62753f:2"> form is a function </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/glossary.html#term-decorator" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e49b6a64d5cd4ee9a2336b531d3b6acf"><span data-offset-key="e49b6a64d5cd4ee9a2336b531d3b6acf:0">decorator</span></span></a><span data-key="250dcc9085684384ab917af26e1c0dc4"><span data-offset-key="250dcc9085684384ab917af26e1c0dc4:0"> ‚Äì see </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/compound_stmts.html#function" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1e6f2d0c251d4458934402a75ad230be"><span data-offset-key="1e6f2d0c251d4458934402a75ad230be:0">Function definitions</span></span></a><span data-key="587c72161ced4349b407ec470e1200cc"><span data-offset-key="587c72161ced4349b407ec470e1200cc:0"> for details. A class method can be called either on the class (such as </span><span data-offset-key="587c72161ced4349b407ec470e1200cc:1">`C.f()`</span><span data-offset-key="587c72161ced4349b407ec470e1200cc:2">) or on an instance (such as </span><span data-offset-key="587c72161ced4349b407ec470e1200cc:3">`C().f()`</span><span data-offset-key="587c72161ced4349b407ec470e1200cc:4">). The instance is ignored except for its class. If a class method is called for a derived class, the derived class object is passed as the implied first argument. Class methods are different than C++ or Java static methods. If you want those, see </span><span data-offset-key="587c72161ced4349b407ec470e1200cc:5">`[staticmethod()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#staticmethod>)`</span><span data-offset-key="587c72161ced4349b407ec470e1200cc:6"> in this section. For more information on class methods, see </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#types" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6479a43033484c248d156b6eb08f6e04"><span data-offset-key="6479a43033484c248d156b6eb08f6e04:0">The standard type hierarchy</span></span></a><span data-key="d0b7d9396d81429c9ca87ca3e6463119"><span data-offset-key="d0b7d9396d81429c9ca87ca3e6463119:0">. </span><span data-offset-key="d0b7d9396d81429c9ca87ca3e6463119:1">*Changed in version 3.9:*</span><span data-offset-key="d0b7d9396d81429c9ca87ca3e6463119:2"> Class methods can now wrap other </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/glossary.html#term-descriptor" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="73a04c5456b94179823418f60c311970"><span data-offset-key="73a04c5456b94179823418f60c311970:0">descriptors</span></span></a><span data-key="cac425fbc4be4e5f91b3dc9c20ee9108"><span data-offset-key="cac425fbc4be4e5f91b3dc9c20ee9108:0"> such as </span><span data-offset-key="cac425fbc4be4e5f91b3dc9c20ee9108:1">`[property()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#property>)`</span><span data-offset-key="cac425fbc4be4e5f91b3dc9c20ee9108:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc"><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:0">**`compile`**</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:2">*source*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:3">, </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:4">*filename*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:5">, </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:6">*mode*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:7">, </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:8">*flags=0*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:9">, </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:10">*dont\_inherit=False*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:11">, </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:12">*optimize=-1*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:13">)Compile the </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:14">*source*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:15"> into a code or AST object. Code objects can be executed by </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:16">`[exec()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#exec>)`</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:17"> or </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:18">`[eval()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#eval>)`</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:19">. </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:20">*source*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:21"> can either be a normal string, a byte string, or an AST object. Refer to the </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:22">`[ast](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/ast.html#module-ast>)`</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:23"> module documentation for information on how to work with AST objects. The </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:24">*filename*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:25"> argument should give the file from which the code was read; pass some recognizable value if it wasn‚Äôt read from a file (</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:26">`'<string>'`</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:27"> is commonly used). The </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:28">*mode*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:29"> argument specifies what kind of code must be compiled; it can be </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:30">`'exec'`</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:31"> if </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:32">*source*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:33"> consists of a sequence of statements, </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:34">`'eval'`</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:35"> if it consists of a single expression, or </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:36">`'single'`</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:37"> if it consists of a single interactive statement (in the latter case, expression statements that evaluate to something other than </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:38">`None`</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:39"> will be printed). The optional arguments </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:40">*flags*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:41"> and </span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:42">*dont\_inherit*</span><span data-offset-key="350c8aef699c43059d1facd7eff911fc:43"> control which </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/ast.html#ast-compiler-flags" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="fa2d6afa17864732ad7ebd0c7fd581d5"><span data-offset-key="fa2d6afa17864732ad7ebd0c7fd581d5:0">compiler options</span></span></a><span data-key="30bb1e011aa84a0281cad72e2ed351bd"><span data-offset-key="30bb1e011aa84a0281cad72e2ed351bd:0"> should be activated and which </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#future" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="453417e8504a48bbb50bbf357349adfa"><span data-offset-key="453417e8504a48bbb50bbf357349adfa:0">future features</span></span></a><span data-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b"><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:0"> should be allowed. If neither is present (or both are zero) the code is compiled with the same flags that affect the code that is calling </span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:1">`[compile()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#compile>)`</span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:2">. If the </span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:3">*flags*</span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:4"> argument is given and </span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:5">*dont\_inherit*</span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:6"> is not (or is zero) then the compiler options and the future statements specified by the </span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:7">*flags*</span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:8"> argument are used in addition to those that would be used anyway. If </span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:9">*dont\_inherit*</span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:10"> is a non-zero integer then the </span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:11">*flags*</span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:12"> argument is it ‚Äì the flags (future features and compiler options) in the surrounding code are ignored. Compiler options and future statements are specified by bits which can be bitwise ORed together to specify multiple options. The bitfield required to specify a given future feature can be found as the </span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:13">`compiler_flag`</span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:14"> attribute on the </span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:15">`_Feature`</span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:16"> instance in the </span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:17">`[__future__](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/__future__.html#module-__future__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="362e5e71fa1c435d93f401252703af9b:18"> module. </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/ast.html#ast-compiler-flags" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="485175ccb48a4c60906d482ba1f5f9cf"><span data-offset-key="485175ccb48a4c60906d482ba1f5f9cf:0">Compiler flags</span></span></a><span data-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a"><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:0"> can be found in </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:1">`[ast](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/ast.html#module-ast>)`</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:2"> module, with </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:3">`PyCF_`</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:4"> prefix. The argument </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:5">*optimize*</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:6"> specifies the optimization level of the compiler; the default value of </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:7">`-1`</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:8"> selects the optimization level of the interpreter as given by </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:9">`[-O](<https://docs.python.org/3/using/cmdline.html#cmdoption-o>)`</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:10"> options. Explicit levels are </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:11">`0`</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:12"> (no optimization; </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:13">`__debug__`</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:14"> is true), </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:15">`1`</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:16"> (asserts are removed, </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:17">`__debug__`</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:18"> is false) or </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:19">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:20"> (docstrings are removed too). This function raises </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:21">`[SyntaxError](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/exceptions.html#SyntaxError>)`</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:22"> if the compiled source is invalid, and </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:23">`[ValueError](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/exceptions.html#ValueError>)`</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:24"> if the source contains null bytes. If you want to parse Python code into its AST representation, see </span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:25">`[ast.parse()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/ast.html#ast.parse>)`</span><span data-offset-key="4374e07d6d75480aac44f56bfb765a7a:26">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dfb410cfb7d74c20a861b062219a69ff"><span data-offset-key="dfb410cfb7d74c20a861b062219a69ff:0">Raises an </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#auditing" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="dbbbccc0933f47ec93b7d0640e06c3f3"><span data-offset-key="dbbbccc0933f47ec93b7d0640e06c3f3:0">auditing event</span></span></a><span data-key="72ea27c13b5b4f049fea7e917d4a59f4"><span data-offset-key="72ea27c13b5b4f049fea7e917d4a59f4:0"> </span><span data-offset-key="72ea27c13b5b4f049fea7e917d4a59f4:1">`compile`</span><span data-offset-key="72ea27c13b5b4f049fea7e917d4a59f4:2"> with arguments </span><span data-offset-key="72ea27c13b5b4f049fea7e917d4a59f4:3">`source`</span><span data-offset-key="72ea27c13b5b4f049fea7e917d4a59f4:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="72ea27c13b5b4f049fea7e917d4a59f4:5">`filename`</span><span data-offset-key="72ea27c13b5b4f049fea7e917d4a59f4:6">. This event may also be raised by implicit compilation.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2"><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:0">**Note**</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:1"> When compiling a string with multi-line code in </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:2">`'single'`</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:3"> or </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:4">`'eval'`</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:5"> mode, input must be terminated by at least one newline character. This is to facilitate detection of incomplete and complete statements in the </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:6">`[code](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/code.html#module-code>)`</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:7"> module. </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:8">**Warning**</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:9"> It is possible to crash the Python interpreter with a sufficiently large/complex string when compiling to an AST object due to stack depth limitations in Python‚Äôs AST compiler. </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:10">*Changed in version 3.2:*</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:11"> Allowed use of Windows and Mac newlines. Also input in </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:12">`'exec'`</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:13"> mode does not have to end in a newline anymore. Added the </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:14">*optimize*</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:15"> parameter. </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:16">*Changed in version 3.5:*</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:17"> Previously, </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:18">`[TypeError](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/exceptions.html#TypeError>)`</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:19"> was raised when null bytes were encountered in </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:20">*source*</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:21">. </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:22">*New in version 3.8:*</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:23"> </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:24">`ast.PyCF_ALLOW_TOP_LEVEL_AWAIT`</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:25"> can now be passed in flags to enable support for top-level </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:26">`await`</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:27">, </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:28">`async for`</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:29">, and </span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:30">`async with`</span><span data-offset-key="b21932e25b684f7f8b1cc4bf0af578e2:31">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d"><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:0">*class*</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:1"> </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:2">**`complex`**</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:3">(\[</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:4">*real*</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:5">\[, </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:6">*imag*</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:7">\]\])Return a complex number with the value </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:8">*real*</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:9"> + \*imag\*\*1j or convert a string or number to a complex number. If the first parameter is a string, it will be interpreted as a complex number and the function must be called without a second parameter. The second parameter can never be a string. Each argument may be any numeric type (including complex). If </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:10">*imag*</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:11"> is omitted, it defaults to zero and the constructor serves as a numeric conversion like </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:12">`[int](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int>)`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:13"> and </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:14">`[float](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#float>)`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:15">. If both arguments are omitted, returns </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:16">`0j`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:17">. For a general Python object </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:18">`x`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:19">, </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:20">`complex(x)`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:21"> delegates to </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:22">`x.__complex__()`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:23">. If </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:24">`__complex__()`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:25"> is not defined then it falls back to </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:26">`[__float__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__float__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:27">. If </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:28">`__float__()`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:29"> is not defined then it falls back to </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:30">`[__index__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__index__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:31">. </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:32">**Note**</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:33"> When converting from a string, the string must not contain whitespace around the central </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:34">`+`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:35"> or </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:36">`-`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:37"> operator. For example, </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:38">`complex('1+2j')`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:39"> is fine, but </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:40">`complex('1 + 2j')`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:41"> raises </span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:42">`[ValueError](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/exceptions.html#ValueError>)`</span><span data-offset-key="c9355b9dd04740eaaae5c6bf570be96d:43">. The complex type is described in </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#typesnumeric" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0e77b9bd27ca433fa7b9f17020e7bf5a"><span data-offset-key="0e77b9bd27ca433fa7b9f17020e7bf5a:0">Numeric Types ‚Äî int, float, complex</span></span></a><span data-key="ab03931bf9f54f85baae5c1d2746d64e"><span data-offset-key="ab03931bf9f54f85baae5c1d2746d64e:0">. </span><span data-offset-key="ab03931bf9f54f85baae5c1d2746d64e:1">*Changed in version 3.6:*</span><span data-offset-key="ab03931bf9f54f85baae5c1d2746d64e:2"> Grouping digits with underscores as in code literals is allowed. </span><span data-offset-key="ab03931bf9f54f85baae5c1d2746d64e:3">*Changed in version 3.8:*</span><span data-offset-key="ab03931bf9f54f85baae5c1d2746d64e:4"> Falls back to </span><span data-offset-key="ab03931bf9f54f85baae5c1d2746d64e:5">`[__index__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__index__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="ab03931bf9f54f85baae5c1d2746d64e:6"> if </span><span data-offset-key="ab03931bf9f54f85baae5c1d2746d64e:7">`[__complex__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__complex__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="ab03931bf9f54f85baae5c1d2746d64e:8"> and </span><span data-offset-key="ab03931bf9f54f85baae5c1d2746d64e:9">`[__float__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__float__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="ab03931bf9f54f85baae5c1d2746d64e:10"> are not defined.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee"><span data-offset-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee:0">**`delattr`**</span><span data-offset-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee:2">*object*</span><span data-offset-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee:3">, </span><span data-offset-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee:4">*name*</span><span data-offset-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee:5">)This is a relative of </span><span data-offset-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee:6">`[setattr()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#setattr>)`</span><span data-offset-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee:7">. The arguments are an object and a string. The string must be the name of one of the object‚Äôs attributes. The function deletes the named attribute, provided the object allows it. For example, </span><span data-offset-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee:8">`delattr(x, 'foobar')`</span><span data-offset-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee:9"> is equivalent to </span><span data-offset-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee:10">`del x.foobar`</span><span data-offset-key="f50faf84788b44f1a1ebc9a6361aecee:11">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a"><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:0">*class*</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:1"> </span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:2">**`dict`**</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:3">(\*\*</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:4">*kwarg*</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:5">)</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:6">*class*</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:7"> </span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:8">**`dict`**</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:9">(</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:10">*mapping*</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:11">, \*\*</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:12">*kwarg*</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:13">)</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:14">*class*</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:15"> </span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:16">**`dict`**</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:17">(</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:18">*iterable*</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:19">, \*\*</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:20">*kwarg*</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:21">)Create a new dictionary. The </span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:22">`[dict](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#dict>)`</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:23"> object is the dictionary class. See </span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:24">`[dict](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#dict>)`</span><span data-offset-key="fd3bed150de241c2924c6f9e0ab8245a:25"> and </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#typesmapping" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cac69fae6ff14d1eb144c206a39e772c"><span data-offset-key="cac69fae6ff14d1eb144c206a39e772c:0">Mapping Types ‚Äî dict</span></span></a><span data-key="c91a259c13144f65844e11b1f4434ce7"><span data-offset-key="c91a259c13144f65844e11b1f4434ce7:0"> for documentation about this class. For other containers see the built-in </span><span data-offset-key="c91a259c13144f65844e11b1f4434ce7:1">`[list](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#list>)`</span><span data-offset-key="c91a259c13144f65844e11b1f4434ce7:2">, </span><span data-offset-key="c91a259c13144f65844e11b1f4434ce7:3">`[set](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#set>)`</span><span data-offset-key="c91a259c13144f65844e11b1f4434ce7:4">, and </span><span data-offset-key="c91a259c13144f65844e11b1f4434ce7:5">`[tuple](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#tuple>)`</span><span data-offset-key="c91a259c13144f65844e11b1f4434ce7:6"> classes, as well as the </span><span data-offset-key="c91a259c13144f65844e11b1f4434ce7:7">`[collections](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/collections.html#module-collections>)`</span><span data-offset-key="c91a259c13144f65844e11b1f4434ce7:8"> module.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a"><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:0">**`dir`**</span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:1">(\[</span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:2">*object*</span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:3">\])Without arguments, return the list of names in the current local scope. With an argument, attempt to return a list of valid attributes for that object. If the object has a method named </span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:4">`[__dir__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__dir__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:5">, this method will be called and must return the list of attributes. This allows objects that implement a custom </span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:6">`[__getattr__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__getattr__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:7"> or </span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:8">`[__getattribute__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__getattribute__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:9"> function to customize the way </span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:10">`[dir()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#dir>)`</span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:11"> reports their attributes. If the object does not provide </span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:12">`[__dir__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__dir__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:13">, the function tries its best to gather information from the object‚Äôs </span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:14">`[__dict__](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#object.__dict__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:15"> attribute, if defined, and from its type object. The resulting list is not necessarily complete, and may be inaccurate when the object has a custom </span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:16">`[__getattr__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__getattr__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:17">. The default </span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:18">`[dir()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#dir>)`</span><span data-offset-key="67dfe3b9a3e44e77af7f78ae0ca0075a:19"> mechanism behaves differently with different types of objects, as it attempts to produce the most relevant, rather than complete, information: ‚Ä¢ If the object is a module object, the list contains the names of the module‚Äôs attributes. ‚Ä¢ If the object is a type or class object, the list contains the names of its attributes, and recursively of the attributes of its bases. ‚Ä¢ Otherwise, the list contains the object‚Äôs attributes‚Äô names, the names of its class‚Äôs attributes, and recursively of the attributes of its class‚Äôs base classes. The resulting list is sorted alphabetically. For example:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="56fa0fe049d443fdb43b931bb6a37d13"><span data-offset-key="56fa0fe049d443fdb43b931bb6a37d13:0">\*\*</span><span data-offset-key="56fa0fe049d443fdb43b931bb6a37d13:1">`>>> import** **struct>>>** dir() *# show the names in the module namespace* ['__builtins__', '__name__', 'struct'] **>>>** dir(struct) *# show the names in the struct module* ['Struct', '__all__', '__builtins__', '__cached__', '__doc__', '__file__', '__initializing__', '__loader__', '__name__', '__package__', '_clearcache', 'calcsize', 'error', 'pack', 'pack_into', 'unpack', 'unpack_from'] **>>> class** **Shape**: **...** **def** __dir__(self): **...** **return** ['area', 'perimeter', 'location'] **>>>** s = Shape() **>>>** dir(s) ['area', 'location', 'perimeter']`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="164d5d4bfca6450d8f38119c633989a3"><span data-offset-key="164d5d4bfca6450d8f38119c633989a3:0">**Note**</span><span data-offset-key="164d5d4bfca6450d8f38119c633989a3:1"> Because </span><span data-offset-key="164d5d4bfca6450d8f38119c633989a3:2">`[dir()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#dir>)`</span><span data-offset-key="164d5d4bfca6450d8f38119c633989a3:3"> is supplied primarily as a convenience for use at an interactive prompt, it tries to supply an interesting set of names more than it tries to supply a rigorously or consistently defined set of names, and its detailed behavior may change across releases. For example, metaclass attributes are not in the result list when the argument is a class.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352"><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:0">**`divmod`**</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:2">*a*</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:3">, </span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:4">*b*</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:5">)Take two (non complex) numbers as arguments and return a pair of numbers consisting of their quotient and remainder when using integer division. With mixed operand types, the rules for binary arithmetic operators apply. For integers, the result is the same as </span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:6">`(a // b, a % b)`</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:7">. For floating point numbers the result is </span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:8">`(q, a % b)`</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:9">, where </span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:10">*q*</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:11"> is usually </span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:12">`math.floor(a / b)`</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:13"> but may be 1 less than that. In any case </span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:14">`q * b + a % b`</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:15"> is very close to </span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:16">*a*</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:17">, if </span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:18">`a % b`</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:19"> is non-zero it has the same sign as </span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:20">*b*</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:21">, and </span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:22">`0 <= abs(a % b) < abs(b)`</span><span data-offset-key="ece319802b714865a9e9acb3e32cf352:23">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="566c8e0a178a4090bd2eb7053e4b415d"><span data-offset-key="566c8e0a178a4090bd2eb7053e4b415d:0">**`enumerate`**</span><span data-offset-key="566c8e0a178a4090bd2eb7053e4b415d:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="566c8e0a178a4090bd2eb7053e4b415d:2">*iterable*</span><span data-offset-key="566c8e0a178a4090bd2eb7053e4b415d:3">, </span><span data-offset-key="566c8e0a178a4090bd2eb7053e4b415d:4">*start=0*</span><span data-offset-key="566c8e0a178a4090bd2eb7053e4b415d:5">)Return an enumerate object. </span><span data-offset-key="566c8e0a178a4090bd2eb7053e4b415d:6">*iterable*</span><span data-offset-key="566c8e0a178a4090bd2eb7053e4b415d:7"> must be a sequence, an </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/glossary.html#term-iterator" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="14270fd51aaa48b2aea0ea576f8f457e"><span data-offset-key="14270fd51aaa48b2aea0ea576f8f457e:0">iterator</span></span></a><span data-key="cab3b7ad5d684bce8db2527bb71f6617"><span data-offset-key="cab3b7ad5d684bce8db2527bb71f6617:0">, or some other object which supports iteration. The </span><span data-offset-key="cab3b7ad5d684bce8db2527bb71f6617:1">`[__next__()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#iterator.__next__>)`</span><span data-offset-key="cab3b7ad5d684bce8db2527bb71f6617:2"> method of the iterator returned by </span><span data-offset-key="cab3b7ad5d684bce8db2527bb71f6617:3">`[enumerate()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#enumerate>)`</span><span data-offset-key="cab3b7ad5d684bce8db2527bb71f6617:4"> returns a tuple containing a count (from </span><span data-offset-key="cab3b7ad5d684bce8db2527bb71f6617:5">*start*</span><span data-offset-key="cab3b7ad5d684bce8db2527bb71f6617:6"> which defaults to 0) and the values obtained from iterating over </span><span data-offset-key="cab3b7ad5d684bce8db2527bb71f6617:7">*iterable*</span><span data-offset-key="cab3b7ad5d684bce8db2527bb71f6617:8">.&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8620fa6414994b4086a420e3b8034d07"><span data-offset-key="8620fa6414994b4086a420e3b8034d07:0">\*\*</span><span data-offset-key="8620fa6414994b4086a420e3b8034d07:1">`>>>** seasons = ['Spring', 'Summer', 'Fall', 'Winter'] **>>>** list(enumerate(seasons)) [(0, 'Spring'), (1, 'Summer'), (2, 'Fall'), (3, 'Winter')] **>>>** list(enumerate(seasons, start=1)) [(1, 'Spring'), (2, 'Summer'), (3, 'Fall'), (4, 'Winter')]`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2404c6b978fa4494a7a200a9f49d8957"><span data-offset-key="2404c6b978fa4494a7a200a9f49d8957:0">Equivalent to:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b62466a6aec44fdfa5d2950259a0655c"><span data-offset-key="b62466a6aec44fdfa5d2950259a0655c:0">\*\*</span><span data-offset-key="b62466a6aec44fdfa5d2950259a0655c:1">`def** enumerate(sequence, start=0): n = start **for** elem **in** sequence: **yield** n, elem n += 1`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e"><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:0">**`eval`**</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:2">*expression*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:3">\[, </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:4">*globals*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:5">\[, </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:6">*locals*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:7">\]\])The arguments are a string and optional globals and locals. If provided, </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:8">*globals*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:9"> must be a dictionary. If provided, </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:10">*locals*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:11"> can be any mapping object. The </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:12">*expression*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:13"> argument is parsed and evaluated as a Python expression (technically speaking, a condition list) using the </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:14">*globals*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:15"> and </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:16">*locals*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:17"> dictionaries as global and local namespace. If the </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:18">*globals*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:19"> dictionary is present and does not contain a value for the key </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:20">`__builtins__`</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:21">, a reference to the dictionary of the built-in module </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:22">`[builtins](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/builtins.html#module-builtins>)`</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:23"> is inserted under that key before </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:24">*expression*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:25"> is parsed. This means that </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:26">*expression*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:27"> normally has full access to the standard </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:28">`[builtins](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/builtins.html#module-builtins>)`</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:29"> module and restricted environments are propagated. If the </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:30">*locals*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:31"> dictionary is omitted it defaults to the </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:32">*globals*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:33"> dictionary. If both dictionaries are omitted, the expression is executed with the </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:34">*globals*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:35"> and </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:36">*locals*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:37"> in the environment where </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:38">`[eval()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#eval>)`</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:39"> is called. Note, </span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:40">*eval()*</span><span data-offset-key="d44dfd8942ff467fbb982cc13366357e:41"> does not have access to the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/glossary.html#term-nested-scope" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8a6ab346e761443ab9cf3b7d13412958"><span data-offset-key="8a6ab346e761443ab9cf3b7d13412958:0">nested scopes</span></span></a><span data-key="ec4bf7e0ab964200839b22771c9b0894"><span data-offset-key="ec4bf7e0ab964200839b22771c9b0894:0"> (non-locals) in the enclosing environment. The return value is the result of the evaluated expression. Syntax errors are reported as exceptions. Example:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f1967232c9454257ab5b9edc0719671a"><span data-offset-key="f1967232c9454257ab5b9edc0719671a:0">\*\*</span><span data-offset-key="f1967232c9454257ab5b9edc0719671a:1">`>>>** x = 1 **>>>** eval('x+1') 2`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244"><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:0">This function can also be used to execute arbitrary code objects (such as those created by </span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:1">`[compile()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#compile>)`</span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:2">). In this case pass a code object instead of a string. If the code object has been compiled with </span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:3">`'exec'`</span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:4"> as the </span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:5">*mode*</span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:6"> argument, </span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:7">`[eval()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#eval>)`</span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:8">‚Äôs return value will be </span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:9">`None`</span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:10">. Hints: dynamic execution of statements is supported by the </span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:11">`[exec()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#exec>)`</span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:12"> function. The </span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:13">`[globals()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#globals>)`</span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:14"> and </span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:15">`[locals()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#locals>)`</span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:16"> functions returns the current global and local dictionary, respectively, which may be useful to pass around for use by </span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:17">`[eval()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#eval>)`</span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:18"> or </span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:19">`[exec()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#exec>)`</span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:20">. See </span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:21">`[ast.literal_eval()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/ast.html#ast.literal_eval>)`</span><span data-offset-key="5c423a7b89f947f88a244847d0c6d244:22"> for a function that can safely evaluate strings with expressions containing only literals.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="49e4629e4b87483884ac039895c10023"><span data-offset-key="49e4629e4b87483884ac039895c10023:0">Raises an </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#auditing" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1a06ae5f2b1e433b8394f27b5e17a373"><span data-offset-key="1a06ae5f2b1e433b8394f27b5e17a373:0">auditing event</span></span></a><span data-key="095e098e1c1c486c8298e4b4767a5cd0"><span data-offset-key="095e098e1c1c486c8298e4b4767a5cd0:0"> </span><span data-offset-key="095e098e1c1c486c8298e4b4767a5cd0:1">`exec`</span><span data-offset-key="095e098e1c1c486c8298e4b4767a5cd0:2"> with the code object as the argument. Code compilation events may also be raised.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="87db2332f1c5472c9f341e5a96ec8b29"><span data-offset-key="87db2332f1c5472c9f341e5a96ec8b29:0">**`exec`**</span><span data-offset-key="87db2332f1c5472c9f341e5a96ec8b29:1">(</span><span data-offset-key="87db2332f1c5472c9f341e5a96ec8b29:2">*object*</span><span data-offset-key="87db2332f1c5472c9f341e5a96ec8b29:3">\[, </span><span data-offset-key="87db2332f1c5472c9f341e5a96ec8b29:4">*globals*</span><span data-offset-key="87db2332f1c5472c9f341e5a96ec8b29:5">\[, </span><span data-offset-key="87db2332f1c5472c9f341e5a96ec8b29:6">*locals*</span><span data-offset-key="87db2332f1c5472c9f341e5a96ec8b29:7">\]\])This function supports dynamic execution of Python code. </span><span data-offset-key="87db2332f1c5472c9f341e5a96ec8b29:8">*object*</span><span data-offset-key="87db2332f1c5472c9f341e5a96ec8b29:9"> must be either a string or a code object. If it is a string, the string is parsed as a suite of Python statements which is then executed (unless a syntax error occurs). </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#id2" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c4b2be92e0494694af5e963726877623"><span data-offset-key="c4b2be92e0494694af5e963726877623:0">1</span></span></a><span data-key="bc455cbe9e0543458b62a0134e9ab983"><span data-offset-key="bc455cbe9e0543458b62a0134e9ab983:0"> If it is a code object, it is simply executed. In all cases, the code that‚Äôs executed is expected to be valid as file input (see the section ‚ÄúFile input‚Äù in the Reference Manual). Be aware that the </span><span data-offset-key="bc455cbe9e0543458b62a0134e9ab983:1">`[nonlocal](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#nonlocal>)`</span><span data-offset-key="bc455cbe9e0543458b62a0134e9ab983:2">, </span><span data-offset-key="bc455cbe9e0543458b62a0134e9ab983:3">`[yield](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#yield>)`</span><span data-offset-key="bc455cbe9e0543458b62a0134e9ab983:4">, and </span><span data-offset-key="bc455cbe9e0543458b62a0134e9ab983:5">`[return](<https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#return>)`</span><span data-offset-key="bc455cbe9e0543458b62a0134e9ab983:6"> statements may not be used outside of function definitions even within the context of code passed to the </span><span data-offset-key="bc455cbe9e0543458b62a0134e9ab983:7">`[exec()](<https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#exec>)`</span><span data-offset-key="bc455cbe9e0543458b62a0134e9ab983:8"> function. The return value is </span><span data-offset-key="bc455cbe9e0543458b62a0134e9ab983:9">`None`</span><span data-offset-key="bc455cbe9e0543458b62a0134e9ab983:10">. In all cases, if the optional parts are omitted, the code is executed in the current scope.
